std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}}+1 $>$ $>$ ps\+::add\+\_\+dimension (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ \&}]{new\+\_\+dimension }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Add a new dimension to a set of points. 

This function takes a vector of points of dimension N and appends a new coordinate to each point, producing a new vector of points of dimension N+1.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Numeric type of the coordinates (e.\+g., float, double, int). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Current number of dimensions in the input points. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of input points of dimension N. \\
\hline
{\em new\+\_\+dimension} & Vector of values for the new dimension. Must have the same size as {\ttfamily points}. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of points of dimension N+1, with the new dimension appended.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em std\+::runtime\+\_\+errorifthesizeof\`{}points\`{}and\`{}new\+\_\+dimension\`{}donotmatch.} & \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This function creates a new vector of points with an increased dimension count, since the type Point$<$\+T, N$>$ is distinct from \doxylink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T, N+1\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}.
\end{DoxyNote}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}

\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<float>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{z\_values}}\ =\ \{\ 10.0f,\ 20.0f\ \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points3D}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a964f314c19f0b1300d513bce618c5954}{add\_dimension}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}},\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{z\_values}});}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ points3D\ now\ contains\ \{\{1.0f,\ 2.0f,\ 10.0f\}\},\ \{\{3.0f,\ 4.0f,\ 20.0f\}\}}}

\end{DoxyCode}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{angle\_distribution\_neighbors()}{angle\_distribution\_neighbors()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::pair$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::angle\+\_\+distribution\+\_\+neighbors (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{bin\+\_\+width,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{k\+\_\+neighbors = {\ttfamily 8} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute the angular distribution function (ADF) using nearest neighbors. 

The angular distribution function (ADF) measures the distribution of bond angles formed by a point and pairs of its nearest neighbors.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Flat distribution  random uniform points.
\item Peaks at characteristic angles  local order (e.\+g. hexagonal lattice peaks at 60).
\item Depletions  angular avoidance due to constraints or repulsion.
\end{DoxyItemize}


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Numeric type (float, double, ...) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of points (N \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 2) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of points \\
\hline
{\em bin\+\_\+width} & Width of angle bins (in radians) \\
\hline
{\em k\+\_\+neighbors} & Number of neighbors used for angle calculation (default\+: 8) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::pair\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}std\+::vector$<$\+T$>$, std\+::vector$<$\+T$>$\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item First\+: bin centers (angles in radians)
\item Second\+: normalized ADF values
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}

\DoxyCodeLine{}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{dbscan\_clustering()}{dbscan\_clustering()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$ ps\+::dbscan\+\_\+clustering (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{eps,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{min\+\_\+pts }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Density-\/\+Based Spatial Clustering of Applications with Noise (DBSCAN). 

Groups points into clusters based on density\+: a point is a core if it has at least {\ttfamily min\+\_\+pts} neighbors within distance {\ttfamily eps}. Clusters are formed by expanding from core points. Noise points remain unclustered.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (float/double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Input point cloud. \\
\hline
{\em eps} & Neighborhood radius for density check. \\
\hline
{\em min\+\_\+pts} & Minimum neighbors (including self) to be a core point. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of cluster labels (-\/1 = noise, 0..k = cluster IDs).
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{labels}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{dbscan<double,2>}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}},\ 0.05,\ 5);}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
This assigns each 2D point either to a cluster ID or -\/1 (noise).

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{distance\_rejection\_filter()}{distance\_rejection\_filter()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::distance\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{min\+\_\+dist }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Filters a set of points using a greedy distance-\/based rejection. 

Points are added one by one. If a point is at least {\ttfamily min\+\_\+dist} away from all previously accepted points, it is kept. Otherwise, it is rejected.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of candidate points \\
\hline
{\em min\+\_\+dist} & Minimum allowed distance between two accepted points \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ of filtered points
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<float,\ 2>>\ pts\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ps::random<float,\ 2>}}(1000,\ \{\{0,1\},\{0,1\}\});}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{filtered}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_ad1f4a1110a40bf1c6a687182db6b4b94}{ps::distance\_rejection\_filter}}(pts,\ 0.05f);}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Scale\+Fn}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::distance\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter\+\_\+warped (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Scale\+Fn}}}]{scale\+\_\+fn }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Filters points based on spatially-\/varying minimal distance constraints. 

A scale function is used to modulate the minimum allowed distance for each point. The base distance {\ttfamily base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist} is scaled by the value returned by {\ttfamily scale\+\_\+fn(p)}, allowing for adaptive sampling densities.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
{\em Scale\+Fn} & Callable returning a scalar scale factor for a given point\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of candidate points \\
\hline
{\em base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist} & Base minimum allowed distance \\
\hline
{\em scale\+\_\+fn} & Function providing a local scale factor per point \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ A filtered set of points with variable spacing
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{distance\_to\_boundary()}{distance\_to\_boundary()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ ps\+::distance\+\_\+to\+\_\+boundary (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute the distance of each point to the domain boundary. 

The domain is defined by axis-\/aligned ranges in each dimension. For each point, the returned distance is the smallest Euclidean distance to any boundary plane of the domain.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Floating point type. \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the points. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of points to evaluate. \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Vector of size N, where each element is a std\+::pair\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}min, max\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} defining the domain limits in that dimension. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+T$>$ Distances of each point to the nearest domain boundary.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
This assumes the domain is a rectangular box aligned with the coordinate axes.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<double,\ 2>>\ pts\ =\ \{\ \{0.2,\ 0.8\},\ \{0.9,\ 0.1\}\ \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<std::pair<double,\ double>>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ranges}}\ =\ \{\ \{0.0,\ 1.0\},\ \{0.0,\ 1.0\}\ \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{distances}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a9a824a8963ef7b15c01da0f1f9c90eee}{distance\_to\_boundary}}(pts,\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ranges}});}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ distances[0]\ -\/>\ 0.2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ distances[1]\ -\/>\ 0.1}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Func}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::filter\+\_\+points\+\_\+function (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Func}}}]{fn }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Filters points using a user-\/provided function. 

Keeps only the points for which the provided function {\ttfamily fn(p)} does not return zero. This can be used to apply custom masks, implicit surface functions, etc.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Numeric type for coordinates. \\
\hline
{\em N} & Number of dimensions. \\
\hline
{\em Func} & Callable that takes a Point$<$\+T, N$>$ and returns a value convertible to T.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of input points. \\
\hline
{\em fn} & Unary function that returns a non-\/zero value if the point should be kept.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of filtered points.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}

 \Hypertarget{namespaceps_a91a0bac33731ed899845c6081c117db2}\label{namespaceps_a91a0bac33731ed899845c6081c117db2} 
\index{ps@{ps}!first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared@{first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared}}
\index{first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared@{first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared()}{first\_neighbor\_distance\_squared()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ ps\+::first\+\_\+neighbor\+\_\+distance\+\_\+squared (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Computes the squared distance to the nearest neighbor for each point. 

This function builds a KD-\/tree from a given set of N-\/dimensional points and computes, for each point, the squared distance to its closest neighbor.

The KD-\/tree search uses {\ttfamily nanoflann} for efficient nearest neighbor queries.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of each point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of N-\/dimensional points. Note\+:\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} This vector is passed by non-\/const reference because the KD-\/tree adaptor may require mutable access, but the function does not modify the contents.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector containing the squared distances to the first neighbor for each point, in the same order as the input points.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{function\_rejection\_filter()}{function\_rejection\_filter()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Density\+Fn}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::function\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Density\+Fn}}}]{density\+\_\+fn,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Filters points based on a spatial probability (density) function. 

Each point is accepted with a probability given by {\ttfamily density\+\_\+fn(p)}, which should return a value in \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}. This is useful for sampling from a non-\/uniform spatial distribution.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
{\em Density\+Fn} & Callable type with signature {\ttfamily T(const \doxylink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T, N\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\&)} \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Input candidate points \\
\hline
{\em density\+\_\+fn} & Function returning acceptance probability for each point \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional random seed for reproducibility \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ of accepted points
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{field}}\ =\ [](\textcolor{keyword}{const}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point<float,\ 2>}}\&\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}})\ \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \textcolor{keywordflow}{return}\ 0.5f\ +\ 0.5f\ *\ std::sin(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[0]\ *\ 10.0f);\ \textcolor{comment}{//\ Spatial\ density}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}

\end{DoxyCode}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{gaussian\_clusters()}{gaussian\_clusters()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::gaussian\+\_\+clusters (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{cluster\+\_\+count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{points\+\_\+per\+\_\+cluster,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{spread,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates clustered points around random centers uniformly sampled in a bounding box. 

Cluster centers are randomly sampled within the provided {\ttfamily axis\+\_\+ranges}, and each cluster then has {\ttfamily points\+\_\+per\+\_\+cluster} points sampled from a Gaussian distribution centered at the cluster\textquotesingle{}s location, with a specified standard deviation {\ttfamily spread}.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em cluster\+\_\+count} & Number of cluster centers to generate \\
\hline
{\em points\+\_\+per\+\_\+cluster} & Number of points per cluster \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Axis-\/aligned bounding box ranges for each dimension \\
\hline
{\em spread} & Standard deviation of the Gaussian spread \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional random seed \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ A vector of clustered points
\end{DoxyReturn}

\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ 5,\ 100,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{\{\{0,1\},\ \{0,1\}\}\},\ 0.03f}
\DoxyCodeLine{);}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::gaussian\+\_\+clusters (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$}]{cluster\+\_\+centers,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{points\+\_\+per\+\_\+cluster,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{spread,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates clustered points around provided cluster centers using a Gaussian distribution. 

For each cluster center, this function generates {\ttfamily points\+\_\+per\+\_\+cluster} points where each coordinate is sampled from a normal distribution centered at the coordinate of the cluster center with standard deviation {\ttfamily spread}.

{\em spread} & Standard deviation of the Gaussian spread \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional random seed \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ A vector of clustered points

\index{halton@{halton}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{halton()}{halton()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::halton (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates a set of quasi-\/random points using the Halton sequence in N dimensions. 

This function generates {\ttfamily count} points in the unit hypercube using the Halton sequence, then rescales them to fit within the specified axis-\/aligned bounding box. An optional {\ttfamily seed} is used as a starting index offset (i.\+e., a shift) in the sequence to decorrelate multiple calls.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & Number of points to generate \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Axis-\/aligned bounding box for each dimension, as min/max pairs \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional seed that offsets the sequence start index \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ The generated Halton points rescaled to the bounding box
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ 1000,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{\{\{0,\ 1\},\ \{0,\ 1\}\}\},\ 42}
\DoxyCodeLine{);}

Generates a set of quasi-\/random points using the Hammersley sequence in N dimensions. 

This function generates {\ttfamily count} points in the unit hypercube using the Hammersley sequence, then rescales them to fit within the specified axis-\/aligned bounding box. An optional {\ttfamily seed} can be used as a starting index offset (i.\+e., a shift) to decorrelate multiple calls or introduce variation.

\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\

\index{importance\_resampling@{importance\_resampling}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{importance\_resampling()}{importance\_resampling()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Density\+Fn}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::importance\+\_\+resampling (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{oversampling\+\_\+ratio,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Density\+Fn}}}]{density\+\_\+fn,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates a point set via importance resampling from a quasi-\/random oversampled grid. 

This function uses a Halton sequence to create an oversampled set of candidate points in the domain. Each point is assigned a weight based on the provided density function. A discrete distribution is then used to resample {\ttfamily count} points according to these weights.

The higher the {\ttfamily oversampling\+\_\+ratio}, the better the approximation to the target density, at the cost of performance.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
{\em Density\+Fn} & A callable with signature {\ttfamily T(const \doxylink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}T, N\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}\&)} returning a non-\/negative density value \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & Number of points to return after resampling \\
\hline
{\em oversampling\+\_\+ratio} & Number of candidate points to generate as a multiple of {\ttfamily count} \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Axis-\/aligned bounding box defining the domain of the points \\
\hline
{\em density\+\_\+fn} & Function mapping a point to a (non-\/negative) density value \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional seed to control the random number generator \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ The resulting resampled point set
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{density}}\ =\ [](\textcolor{keyword}{const}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point<float,\ 2>}}\ \&\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}})\ \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \textcolor{keywordflow}{return}\ std::exp(-\/10.0f\ *\ (\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[0]*\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[0]\ +\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[1]*\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[1]));}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ps::importance\_resampling<float,\ 2>}}(}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ 500,\ 5,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{\{\{-\/1,\ 1\},\ \{-\/1,\ 1\}\}\},\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{density}},\ 42}
\DoxyCodeLine{);}

\end{DoxyCode}

\index{ps@{ps}!jittered\_grid@{jittered\_grid}}
\index{jittered\_grid@{jittered\_grid}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{jittered\_grid()}{jittered\_grid()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::jittered\+\_\+grid (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{jitter\+\_\+amount,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{stagger\+\_\+ratio,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates a point set on a jittered and optionally staggered grid. 

This function divides the domain into a grid and places one point in each selected cell. Each point is jittered within its cell, and staggered offsets may be applied depending on the index of higher-\/dimensional axes. The result is a semi-\/regular sampling pattern with randomness.

Jittering prevents aliasing, and staggering introduces a controlled shift between alternating cells to improve uniformity and avoid alignment artifacts.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & Number of output points (best effort, may be capped by total available cells) \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Axis-\/aligned bounding box defining the sampling domain \\
\hline
{\em jitter\+\_\+amount} & Per-\/dimension jitter factor  \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}. A value of 1.\+0 means full jitter in the cell. \\
\hline
{\em stagger\+\_\+ratio} & Per-\/dimension stagger ratio, indicating how much to offset points based on higher dimension parity \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional seed for deterministic jittering and shuffling \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ Sampled points
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\DoxyCodeLine{std::array<float,\ 2>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{jitter}}\ =\ \{0.8f,\ 0.8f\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::array<float,\ 2>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{stagger}}\ =\ \{0.2f,\ 0.0f\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}

\end{DoxyCode}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{jittered\_grid()}{jittered\_grid()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::jittered\+\_\+grid (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates a jittered grid of points with full jitter and no stagger. 

This overload defaults to jittering each dimension fully within its cell and applies no staggering. It is equivalent to calling the full version with {\ttfamily jitter\+\_\+amount} filled with 1.\+0 and {\ttfamily stagger\+\_\+ratio} filled with 0.\+0.

\hline

\hline
\end{DoxyParams}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\

\index{ps@{ps}!latin\_hypercube\_sampling@{latin\_hypercube\_sampling}}
\index{latin\_hypercube\_sampling@{latin\_hypercube\_sampling}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{latin\_hypercube\_sampling()}{latin\_hypercube\_sampling()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::latin\+\_\+hypercube\+\_\+sampling (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{sample\+\_\+count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates samples using Latin Hypercube Sampling (LHS). 

This function produces {\ttfamily sample\+\_\+count} evenly stratified samples across each dimension defined in {\ttfamily axis\+\_\+ranges}. Each dimension is divided into equal intervals (strata), and one point is randomly selected from each stratum with added jitter. The strata are randomly permuted across dimensions to avoid correlation.

This method ensures uniform coverage of the space while maintaining randomness, making it useful in Monte Carlo integration, surrogate modeling, and probabilistic sampling.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em sample\+\_\+count} & Number of points to generate \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Array of N (min, max) pairs defining the domain in each dimension \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional seed for reproducible randomness\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ of LHS-\/sampled points
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\end{DoxyCode}

\index{local\_density\_knn@{local\_density\_knn}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{local\_density\_knn()}{local\_density\_knn()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ ps\+::local\+\_\+density\+\_\+knn (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{k = {\ttfamily 8} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute local point density based on k-\/nearest neighbors in N dimensions. 

The density at each point is estimated as\+:  \[
\rho_i = \frac{k}{V_N r_i^N}
\] where (r\+\_\+i) is the distance to the k-\/th nearest neighbor, (V\+\_\+N) is the volume of the unit N-\/ball\+:  \[
V_N = \frac{\pi^{N/2}}{\Gamma(N/2 + 1)}
\] and (\textbackslash{}\+Gamma) is the gamma function. This generalizes to any dimension.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of the points. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of points in N-\/dimensional space. \\
\hline
{\em k} & Number of nearest neighbors to use for density estimation (should be \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}= 1). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Vector of local densities for each point.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<double,3>>\ pts\ =\ ...;\ \textcolor{comment}{//\ 3D\ points}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keywordtype}{size\_t}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{k}}\ =\ 8;}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{densities}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{local\_density\_knn<double,3>}}(pts,\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{k}});}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Works in any dimension (N).
\item High k gives smoother density estimates, low k captures local fluctuations.
\item The resulting density units are points per unit volume in N dimensions.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
 \Hypertarget{namespaceps_a677f90d97b1dcfeaa2ecc299ee37f5bf}\label{namespaceps_a677f90d97b1dcfeaa2ecc299ee37f5bf} 
\index{ps@{ps}!merge\_by\_dimension@{merge\_by\_dimension}}
\index{merge\_by\_dimension@{merge\_by\_dimension}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{merge\_by\_dimension()}{merge\_by\_dimension()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::merge\+\_\+by\+\_\+dimension (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{components }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Reconstructs a list of N-\/dimensional points from N separate coordinate vectors. 

This function takes N vectorseach representing one coordinate axisand combines them into a single vector of N-\/dimensional points. It is the inverse operation of {\ttfamily split\+\_\+by\+\_\+dimension}.

All coordinate vectors must have the same length.

For example, given\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item dimension 0\+: \mbox{[}1, 4, 7\mbox{]}
\item dimension 1\+: \mbox{[}2, 5, 8\mbox{]}
\item dimension 2\+: \mbox{[}3, 6, 9\mbox{]}
\end{DoxyItemize}

The result will be\+: \mbox{[}(1,2,3), (4,5,6), (7,8,9)\mbox{]}


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of each point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em components} & An array of N vectors, each containing values for one coordinate axis.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of N-\/dimensional points reconstructed from the coordinate vectors.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em std\+::invalid\+\_\+argumentifthecoordinatevectorsdonotallhavethesame} & length.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::array<std::vector<float>,\ 3>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{components}}\ =\ \{\{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{1.0f,\ 4.0f,\ 7.0f\},\ \ \textcolor{comment}{//\ x}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{2.0f,\ 5.0f,\ 8.0f\},\ \ \textcolor{comment}{//\ y}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{3.0f,\ 6.0f,\ 9.0f\}\ \ \ \textcolor{comment}{//\ z}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\}\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<float,\ 3>>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a677f90d97b1dcfeaa2ecc299ee37f5bf}{merge\_by\_dimension}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{components}});}

\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}
\Hypertarget{namespaceps_ac29744e12116f882d8a620a3fd02d72d}\label{namespaceps_ac29744e12116f882d8a620a3fd02d72d} 
\index{ps@{ps}!nearest\_neighbors\_indices@{nearest\_neighbors\_indices}}
\index{nearest\_neighbors\_indices@{nearest\_neighbors\_indices}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{nearest\_neighbors\_indices()}{nearest\_neighbors\_indices()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::nearest\+\_\+neighbors\+\_\+indices (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{k\+\_\+neighbors = {\ttfamily 8} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Finds the nearest neighbors for each point in a set. 

This function uses a KD-\/tree to search for the k nearest neighbors of each point in the input set, returning their indices. The search excludes the query point itself.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of each point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of N-\/dimensional points. \\
\hline
{\em k\+\_\+neighbors} & Number of nearest neighbors to return for each point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector where each element is a vector of indices representing the nearest neighbors of the corresponding point in {\ttfamily points}.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The KD-\/tree is rebuilt internally for the search.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<float,\ 3>>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{0.0f,\ 0.0f,\ 0.0f\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{1.0f,\ 0.0f,\ 0.0f\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{0.0f,\ 1.0f,\ 0.0f\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{1.0f,\ 1.0f,\ 0.0f\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{neighbors}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_ac29744e12116f882d8a620a3fd02d72d}{nearest\_neighbors\_indices}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}},\ 2);}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ neighbors[0]\ might\ contain\ \{1,\ 2\}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ neighbors[1]\ might\ contain\ \{0,\ 3\}}}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{ps@{ps}!normalize\_points@{normalize\_points}}
\index{normalize\_points@{normalize\_points}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{normalize\_points()}{normalize\_points()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{void}} ps\+::normalize\+\_\+points (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Normalize the coordinates of a set of points along each axis to the range \mbox{[}0, 1\mbox{]}. 

This function finds the minimum and maximum value for each axis across all points and rescales each coordinate so that the minimum becomes 0 and the maximum becomes 1.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Numeric type of the coordinates (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Number of dimensions in each point. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of points to normalize. The points are modified in place.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
If all points have the same value along a given axis, the corresponding normalized coordinate will be set to 0 for that axis.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<float,\ 3>>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{\{1.0f,\ 5.0f,\ 10.0f\}\},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \{\{3.0f,\ 15.0f,\ 20.0f\}\}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a172358f05108b5cabdac4e43ab309ab2}{normalize\_points}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}});}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ Now\ points\ coordinates\ are\ scaled\ in\ [0,\ 1]\ along\ each\ axis}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 
\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{ps@{ps}!percolation\_clustering@{percolation\_clustering}}
\index{percolation\_clustering@{percolation\_clustering}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{percolation\_clustering()}{percolation\_clustering()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$ ps\+::percolation\+\_\+clustering (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{connection\+\_\+radius }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Analyze percolation clusters from a set of points using a radius-\/based neighbor graph. 

Builds a graph where edges exist if points are within {\ttfamily connection\+\_\+radius}, then finds connected components (clusters).


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Input set of points. \\
\hline
{\em connection\+\_\+radius} & Maximum distance for connectivity between points. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of cluster labels, size = points.\+size(). Label = -\/1 if unassigned.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::vector<Point<double,2>>\ pts\ =\ \{\ \{0.1,0.2\},\ \{0.15,0.22\},\ \{0.9,0.9\}\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{labels}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{analyze\_percolation\_clusters<double,2>}}(pts,\ 0.1);}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ labels\ might\ be\ \{0,0,1\},\ meaning\ the\ first\ two\ form\ a\ cluster,\ third\ is\ separate.}}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{ps@{ps}!poisson\_disk\_sampling@{poisson\_disk\_sampling}}
\index{poisson\_disk\_sampling@{poisson\_disk\_sampling}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{poisson\_disk\_sampling()}{poisson\_disk\_sampling()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Scale\+Fn}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::poisson\+\_\+disk\+\_\+sampling (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Scale\+Fn}}}]{scale\+\_\+fn,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{new\+\_\+points\+\_\+attempts = {\ttfamily 30} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generate a set of Poisson disk samples in N-\/dimensional space, possibly with a warped metric. 

This function uses Bridson\textquotesingle{}s algorithm to generate evenly spaced points according to a minimum base distance, which can be warped using a user-\/defined scaling function (e.\+g., density or metric warping).


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of the sampling space. \\
\hline
{\em Scale\+Fn} & Callable type returning a scaling factor at a given point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & Desired number of points (will attempt to generate up to this many). \\
\hline
{\em ranges} & Coordinate axis ranges (bounding box) for each of the N dimensions. \\
\hline
{\em base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist} & Base minimum distance between any two points (before scaling). \\
\hline
{\em scale\+\_\+fn} & Function that returns a distance scaling factor at a given point. This enables warped-\/space or non-\/uniform Poisson sampling. \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional RNG seed for reproducibility. \\
\hline
{\em new\+\_\+points\+\_\+attempts} & Number of candidate points to try around each active point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ A vector of sample points satisfying the scaled Poisson distance constraint.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ranges}}\ =\ std::array<std::pair<float,\ float>,\ 2>\{\{\ \{0.f,\ 1.f\},\ \{0.f,\ 1.f\}\ \}\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{scale\_fn}}\ =\ [](\textcolor{keyword}{const}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Point<float,\ 2>}}\ \&\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}})\ -\/>\ \textcolor{keywordtype}{float}\ \{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \textcolor{keywordflow}{return}\ 1.0f\ +\ 0.5f\ *\ std::sin(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{p}}[0]\ *\ 6.2831f);\ \ \textcolor{comment}{//\ Vary\ distance\ with\ x}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{poisson\_disk\_sampling<float,\ 2>}}(100,\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{ranges}},\ 0.05f,\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{scale\_fn}},\ 42);}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}
s \Hypertarget{namespaceps_a733f4c50a2eb988509aca40d25e86a39}\label{namespaceps_a733f4c50a2eb988509aca40d25e86a39} 
\index{ps@{ps}!poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution@{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution}}
\index{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution@{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution()}{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_distance\_distribution()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Radius\+Gen}} $>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::poisson\+\_\+disk\+\_\+sampling\+\_\+distance\+\_\+distribution (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{n\+\_\+points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{Radius\+Gen}} \&\&}]{radius\+\_\+gen,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{max\+\_\+attempts = {\ttfamily 30} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generate random points with a variable-\/radius Poisson disk sampling. 

Radius is defined by an input distribution.

This algorithm enforces a minimum separation between points based on radii drawn from a user-\/specified distribution. Two points $p_i$, $p_j$ with radii $r_i$, $r_j$ must satisfy\+:  \[
  \| p_i - p_j \| > r_i + r_j
\]

This produces point sets where local spacing reflects the size distribution\+: many small radii yield dense clusters, while large radii produce local depletion zones.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g. float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of the points. \\
\hline
{\em Radius\+Gen} & Callable returning radii sampled from the target distribution.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em n\+\_\+points} & Number of points to generate. \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Ranges for each axis, defining the sampling domain. \\
\hline
{\em radius\+\_\+gen} & Generator functor/lambda returning the next radius. \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+attempts} & Maximum attempts per point before giving up (controls density). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Vector of generated points satisfying the variable-\/radius exclusion rule.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Larger {\ttfamily max\+\_\+attempts} increases the chance of filling the domain but also increases runtime.
\item For efficiency, use a spatial grid or tree if generating many points.
\item Radii are drawn independently per point; correlations can be introduced by adapting {\ttfamily radius\+\_\+gen}.
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyParagraph}{Example}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{preprocessor}{\#include\ <random>}}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::mt19937\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{rng}}\{std::random\_device\{\}()\};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ 2D\ unit\ square}}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::array<std::pair<double,double>,2>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{box}}\ =\ \{\ \{\ \{0,1\},\ \{0,1\}\ \}\ \};}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{comment}{//\ Log-\/normal\ radius\ distribution}}
\DoxyCodeLine{std::lognormal\_distribution<double>\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{logn}}(0.0,\ 0.5);}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{keyword}{auto}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{points}}\ =\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{variable\_radius\_poisson\_disk<double,2>}}(}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ 200,}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{box}},}
\DoxyCodeLine{\ \ \ \ [\&]()\{\ \textcolor{keywordflow}{return}\ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{logn}}(\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{rng}});\ \}}
\DoxyCodeLine{);}

\end{DoxyCode}

\end{DoxyParagraph}

\index{ps@{ps}!poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform@{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform}}
\index{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform@{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform}!ps@{ps}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform()}{poisson\_disk\_sampling\_uniform()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::poisson\+\_\+disk\+\_\+sampling\+\_\+uniform (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{new\+\_\+points\+\_\+attempts = {\ttfamily 30} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generate uniformly distributed Poisson disk samples in N-\/dimensional space. 

This is a convenience wrapper over {\ttfamily poisson\+\_\+disk\+\_\+sampling} using a constant distance scale (i.\+e., uniform metric).


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of the sampling space.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & Desired number of points (will attempt to generate up to this many). \\
\hline
{\em ranges} & Coordinate axis ranges (bounding box) for each of the N dimensions. \\
\hline
{\em base\+\_\+min\+\_\+dist} & Minimum distance between any two points. \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional RNG seed for reproducibility. \\
\hline
{\em new\+\_\+points\+\_\+attempts} & Number of candidate points to try around each active point.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ A vector of uniformly spaced sample points.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{radial\_distribution()}{radial\_distribution()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::pair$<$ std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::radial\+\_\+distribution (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{bin\+\_\+width,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{max\+\_\+distance }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Compute the normalized radial distribution function g(r). 

The radial distribution function (RDF) describes how the density of points varies as a function of distance from a reference point.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item g(r)  1  uniform / random distribution at distance r
\item g(r) \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>} 1  clustering / aggregation (excess probability of finding neighbors)
\item g(r) \texorpdfstring{$<$}{<} 1  depletion / exclusion (points repel or avoid each other)
\end{DoxyItemize}

This function normalizes the observed pair distances against the expected density in the domain (given by axis\+\_\+ranges).


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Numeric type (float, double, ...) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension of points \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Vector of points \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & Axis-\/aligned domain ranges for each dimension \\
\hline
{\em bin\+\_\+width} & Width of distance bins \\
\hline
{\em max\+\_\+distance} & Maximum distance to consider \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::pair\texorpdfstring{$<$}{<}std\+::vector$<$\+T$>$, std\+::vector$<$\+T$>$\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item First\+: radii (bin centers)
\item Second\+: normalized RDF values g(r)
\end{DoxyItemize}
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{random()}{random()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$typename T , size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ T, N $>$ $>$ ps\+::random (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{size\+\_\+t}]{count,  }\item[{const std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ T, T $>$, N $>$ \&}]{axis\+\_\+ranges,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ unsigned int $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generates a specified number of uniformly distributed random points in N-\/dimensional space. 

This function creates {\ttfamily count} random points where each coordinate is independently sampled from a uniform distribution defined by {\ttfamily axis\+\_\+ranges} per dimension.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & The numeric type for coordinates (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & The dimensionality of the points.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em count} & The number of random points to generate. \\
\hline
{\em axis\+\_\+ranges} & An array of N pairs specifying the min and max range for each axis. \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional seed for the random number generator. If not provided, a nondeterministic random seed is used.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector containing {\ttfamily count} randomly generated points within the specified axis ranges.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyExceptions}{Exceptions}
{\em std\+::invalid\+\_\+argument\+Ifanyaxisrangehasmin$>$max.} & \\
\hline
\end{DoxyExceptions}
\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
The points are generated independently per axis using uniform\+\_\+real\+\_\+distribution.
\end{DoxyNote}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::random\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{float}}}]{keep\+\_\+fraction }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Randomly retains a fraction of the input points. 

This is a convenience overload of {\ttfamily random\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter} that accepts a floating-\/point {\ttfamily keep\+\_\+fraction} instead of an absolute count. Internally, it computes the number of points to retain and calls the count-\/based version.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Input vector of points \\
\hline
{\em keep\+\_\+fraction} & Fraction of points to retain (between 0.\+0 and 1.\+0) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ containing {\ttfamily keep\+\_\+fraction \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} points.\+size()} randomly selected points
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{random\_rejection\_filter()}{random\_rejection\_filter()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , std\+::size\+\_\+t N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::random\+\_\+rejection\+\_\+filter (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ \&}]{points,  }\item[{std\+::size\+\_\+t}]{target\+\_\+count }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Randomly retains a fixed number of points from the input set. 

This function returns a subset of the input points of size {\ttfamily target\+\_\+count}, selected uniformly at random without replacement. If {\ttfamily target\+\_\+count} is greater than or equal to the number of input points, the full input is returned.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float or double) \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimensionality of the space \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em points} & Input vector of points \\
\hline
{\em target\+\_\+count} & Desired number of points in the output ( points.\+size()) \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
std\+::vector$<$\+Point$<$\+T, N$>$$>$ containing {\ttfamily target\+\_\+count} randomly selected points
\end{DoxyReturn}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{random\_walk\_filaments()}{random\_walk\_filaments()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily template$<$\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{typename}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} , \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}} N$>$ \\
std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{structps_1_1Point}{Point}}$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ $>$ ps\+::random\+\_\+walk\+\_\+filaments (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{n\+\_\+filaments,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{filament\+\_\+count,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{step\+\_\+size,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{const}} std\+::array$<$ std\+::pair$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{N}} $>$ \&}]{ranges,  }\item[{std\+::optional$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{unsigned}} \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{int}} $>$}]{seed = {\ttfamily std\+:\+:nullopt},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{persistence = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}(0.8)},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}}]{gaussian\+\_\+sigma = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}}(0)},  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{size\+\_\+t}}}]{gaussian\+\_\+samples = {\ttfamily 0},  }\item[{std\+::vector$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{T}} $>$ \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{p\+\_\+distances = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceps_a10763ef2a872aa9eddb48ea341cd6f69}{nullptr}}} }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}



Generate random walk filaments in N dimensions with optional Gaussian thickness. 

Each filament starts at a random seed and grows step by step, where each step is a random direction with a persistence factor to avoid sharp turns. Around each step, additional points can be sampled from a Gaussian distribution to form a "{}thick"{} filament.


\begin{DoxyTemplParams}{Template Parameters}
{\em T} & Scalar type (e.\+g., float, double). \\
\hline
{\em N} & Dimension. \\
\hline
\end{DoxyTemplParams}

\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em n\+\_\+filaments} & Number of separate filaments. \\
\hline
{\em filament\+\_\+count} & Number of points per filament. \\
\hline
{\em step\+\_\+size} & Average step length. \\
\hline
{\em ranges} & Bounding box for clamping. \\
\hline
{\em seed} & Optional RNG seed. \\
\hline
{\em persistence} & Correlation between steps (0 = totally random, 1 = straight line). \\
\hline
{\em gaussian\+\_\+sigma} & Standard deviation of Gaussian scatter around the filament (0 = no scatter, \texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}0 = thick filament). \\
\hline
{\em gaussian\+\_\+samples} & Number of samples drawn per step for thickness. \\
\hline
{\em p\+\_\+distances} & Optional output vector to store p\+\_\+distances of each point from the filament center (0 for core filament points). \\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
A vector of generated filament points.
\end{DoxyReturn}
 \Hypertarget{namespaceps_a2b8197901114d1c4fd6cfe19efcd3862}\label{namespaceps_a2b8197901114d1c4fd6cfe19efcd3862}
